	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Nobel Prize</h1>

	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>


		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the awards established through <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Nobel" title="Alfred Nobel">Alfred Nobel</a>'s will. For the memorial prize, see <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences</a>. For the unrelated American civil engineering prize, see <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Noble_Prize" title="Alfred Noble Prize">Alfred Noble Prize</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Set of five annual international awards, primarily established in 1895 by Alfred Nobel</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<table class="infobox vevent" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="summary" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: #eedd82;">Nobel Prize</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Prize.png" class="image" title="A golden medallion with an embossed image of Alfred Nobel facing left in profile. To the left of the man is the text &quot;ALFR•&quot; then &quot;NOBEL&quot;, and on the right, the text (smaller) &quot;NAT•&quot; then &quot;MDCCCXXXIII&quot; above, followed by (smaller) &quot;OB•&quot; then &quot;MDCCCXCVI&quot; below."><img alt="A golden medallion with an embossed image of Alfred Nobel facing left in profile. To the left of the man is the text &quot;ALFR•&quot; then &quot;NOBEL&quot;, and on the right, the text (smaller) &quot;NAT•&quot; then &quot;MDCCCXXXIII&quot; above, followed by (smaller) &quot;OB•&quot; then &quot;MDCCCXCVI&quot; below." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Nobel_Prize.png/220px-Nobel_Prize.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="216" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Nobel_Prize.png/330px-Nobel_Prize.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Nobel_Prize.png/440px-Nobel_Prize.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="492" /></a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Awarded for</th><td>Outstanding contributions for humanity in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">peace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">physics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">physiology or medicine</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Country</th><td class="location"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> (all prizes except the Peace Prize)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (Peace Prize only)</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Presented by</th><td class="attendee"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Assembly_at_the_Karolinska_Institute" title="Nobel Assembly at the Karolinska Institute">Nobel Assembly at the Karolinska Institute</a> (Physiology or Medicine)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Committee" title="Norwegian Nobel Committee">Norwegian Nobel Committee</a> (Peace)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences">Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences</a> (Chemistry, Economic Sciences, Physics)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Swedish_Academy" title="Swedish Academy">Swedish Academy</a> (Literature)</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Reward(s)</th><td><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize#Award_money" title="Nobel Prize">Prize money</a> of 9 million <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Krona" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish Krona">SEK</a>, approx. <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a></span>986,000 (2018);<sup id="cite_ref-:0_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><br />a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize#Medals" title="Nobel Prize">medal</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize#Diplomas" title="Nobel Prize">diploma</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">First awarded</th><td>1901<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;119&#160;years ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">1901</span>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Number of laureates</th><td>590 prizes to 935 laureates (as of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nobel_Prize&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-:0_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="width: 33%;">Website</th><td><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://nobelprize.org/">nobelprize<wbr />.org</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Nobel Prize</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>/</a></span></span>, <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">NOH</span>-bel</i></a>; <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">Nobelpriset</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Swedish" title="Help:IPA/Swedish">[nʊˈbɛ̂lːˌpriːsɛt]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a>: <i lang="no">Nobelprisen</i>) is a set of annual international awards bestowed in several categories by <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Swedish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norwegian</a> institutions in recognition of academic, cultural, or scientific advances. The <a href="/wiki/Will_and_testament" title="Will and testament">will</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Swedes" title="Swedes">Swedish</a> chemist, engineer and industrialist <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Nobel" title="Alfred Nobel">Alfred Nobel</a> established the five Nobel prizes in 1895. The prizes in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Peace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Physics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Physiology or Medicine</a> were first awarded in 1901.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The prizes are widely regarded as the most prestigious awards available in their respective fields.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shalev8_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shalev8-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1968, <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Riksbank" title="Sveriges Riksbank">Sveriges Riksbank</a>, Sweden's <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a>, established the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Sveriges Riksbank Prize in Economic Sciences in Memory of Alfred Nobel</a>. The award is based on a donation received by the Nobel Foundation in 1968 from <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Riksbank" title="Sveriges Riksbank">Sveriges Riksbank</a> on the occasion of the bank's 300th anniversary. The first Prize in Economic Sciences was awarded to <a href="/wiki/Ragnar_Frisch" title="Ragnar Frisch">Ragnar Frisch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jan_Tinbergen" title="Jan Tinbergen">Jan Tinbergen</a> in 1969. The Prize in <a href="/wiki/Economic_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic Sciences">Economic Sciences</a> is awarded by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences">Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences</a>, Stockholm, Sweden, according to the same principles as for the Nobel Prizes that have been awarded since 1901.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences">Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences</a> awards the Nobel Prize in Chemistry, the Nobel Prize in Physics, and the Sveriges Riksbank Prize in Economic Sciences in Memory of Alfred Nobel; the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Assembly_at_the_Karolinska_Institute" title="Nobel Assembly at the Karolinska Institute">Nobel Assembly at the Karolinska Institute</a> awards the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine; the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Academy" title="Swedish Academy">Swedish Academy</a> grants the Nobel Prize in Literature; and the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Committee" title="Norwegian Nobel Committee">Norwegian Nobel Committee</a> awards the Nobel Peace Prize.
</p><p>Between 1901 and 2018, the Nobel Prizes (and the Prizes in Economic Sciences, from 1969 on) were awarded 590 times to 935 people and organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> With some receiving the Nobel Prize more than once, this makes a total of 27 organizations and 908 individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The prize ceremonies take place annually in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> (with the exception of the Peace Prize ceremony, which is held in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>). Each recipient (known as a "<a href="/wiki/Laureate" title="Laureate">laureate</a>") receives a gold medal, a <a href="/wiki/Diploma" title="Diploma">diploma</a>, and a sum of money that has been decided by the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Foundation" title="Nobel Foundation">Nobel Foundation</a>. (As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nobel_Prize&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, each prize is worth 9,000,000 <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Krona" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish Krona">SEK</a>, or about <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$935,366</span>, €848,678, or £716,224.<sup id="cite_ref-PrizeAmountRaised_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrizeAmountRaised-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>) Medals made before 1980 were struck in 23-carat gold, and later in 18-carat <a href="/wiki/Electrum" title="Electrum">green gold</a> plated with a 24-carat gold coating.
</p><p>The prize is not awarded posthumously; however, if a person is awarded a prize and dies before receiving it, the prize may still be presented.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc1003_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc1003-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> A prize may not be shared among more than three individuals, although the Nobel Peace Prize can be awarded to organizations of more than three people.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Award_ceremonies"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Award ceremonies</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A black and white photo of a bearded man in his fifties sitting in a chair." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg/170px-AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg/255px-AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg/340px-AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1872" data-file-height="2516" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alfred Nobel had the unpleasant surprise of reading his own obituary, which was titled <i>The merchant of death is dead</i>, in a French newspaper.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Nobel" title="Alfred Nobel">Alfred Nobel</a> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sv-Alfred_Nobel.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/00/Sv-Alfred_Nobel.ogg" class="internal" title="Sv-Alfred Nobel.ogg">listen</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Sv-Alfred_Nobel.ogg" title="File:Sv-Alfred Nobel.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>) was born on 21 October 1833 in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, Sweden, into a family of engineers.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz5_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz5-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He was a <a href="/wiki/Chemist" title="Chemist">chemist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineer" title="Engineer">engineer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Inventor" title="Inventor">inventor</a>. In 1894, Nobel purchased the <a href="/wiki/Bofors" title="Bofors">Bofors</a> iron and steel mill, which he made into a major <a href="/wiki/Weapon" title="Weapon">armaments</a> <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturer</a>. Nobel also invented <a href="/wiki/Ballistite" title="Ballistite">ballistite</a>. This invention was a precursor to many smokeless military explosives, especially the British smokeless powder <a href="/wiki/Cordite" title="Cordite">cordite</a>. As a consequence of his patent claims, Nobel was eventually involved in a <a href="/wiki/Patent_infringement" title="Patent infringement">patent infringement</a> <a href="/wiki/Lawsuit" title="Lawsuit">lawsuit</a> over cordite. Nobel amassed a fortune during his lifetime, with most of his wealth coming from his 355&#160;inventions, of which <a href="/wiki/Dynamite" title="Dynamite">dynamite</a> is the most famous.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz11_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz11-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1888, Nobel was astonished to read his own <a href="/wiki/Obituary" title="Obituary">obituary</a>, titled <i>The merchant of death is dead</i>, in a French newspaper. It was Alfred's brother <a href="/wiki/Ludvig_Nobel" title="Ludvig Nobel">Ludvig</a> who had died; the obituary was eight years premature. The article disconcerted Nobel and made him apprehensive about how he would be remembered. This inspired him to change his <a href="/wiki/Will_and_testament" title="Will and testament">will</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> On 10 December 1896, Alfred Nobel died in his villa in <a href="/wiki/Sanremo" title="Sanremo">San Remo, Italy</a>, from a <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_hemorrhage" class="mw-redirect" title="Cerebral hemorrhage">cerebral haemorrhage</a>. He was 63 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-Sohlman13_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sohlman13-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nobel wrote several wills during his lifetime. He composed the last over a year before he died, signing it at the Swedish–Norwegian Club in Paris on 27 November 1895.<sup id="cite_ref-Sohlman7_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sohlman7-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> To widespread astonishment, Nobel's last will specified that his fortune be used to create a series of prizes for those who confer the "greatest benefit on mankind" in <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">physiology</a> or <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peace" title="Peace">peace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thelocal1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelocal1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Nobel bequeathed 94% of his total assets, 31&#160;million SEK (c. US$186 million, €150 million in 2008), to establish the five Nobel Prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams7_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams7-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NobelFoundationPrizeAmount_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NobelFoundationPrizeAmount-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Owing to skepticism surrounding the will, it was not approved by the <a href="/wiki/Storting" title="Storting">Storting</a> in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> until 26 April 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz13-25_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz13-25-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Executors" class="mw-redirect" title="Executors">executors</a> of the will, <a href="/wiki/Ragnar_Sohlman" title="Ragnar Sohlman">Ragnar Sohlman</a> and Rudolf Lilljequist, formed the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Foundation" title="Nobel Foundation">Nobel Foundation</a> to take care of the fortune and to organise the awarding of prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams7-8_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams7-8-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nobel's instructions named a <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Committee" title="Norwegian Nobel Committee">Norwegian Nobel Committee</a> to award the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace Prize">Peace Prize</a>, the members of whom were appointed shortly after the will was approved in April 1897. Soon thereafter, the other prize-awarding organizations were designated. These were <a href="/wiki/Karolinska_Institute" title="Karolinska Institute">Karolinska Institute</a> on 7 June, the Swedish Academy on 9 June, and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences">Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences</a> on 11 June.<sup id="cite_ref-Crawford1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crawford1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The Nobel Foundation reached an agreement on guidelines for how the prizes should be awarded; and, in 1900, the Nobel Foundation's newly created <a href="/wiki/Statute" title="Statute">statutes</a> were promulgated by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_II_of_Sweden" title="Oscar II of Sweden">King Oscar II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thelocal1_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelocal1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In 1905, the <a href="/wiki/Union_between_Sweden_and_Norway" title="Union between Sweden and Norway">personal union between Sweden and Norway</a> was dissolved.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_Foundation">Nobel Foundation</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_of_Foundation">Formation of Foundation</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Foundation" title="Nobel Foundation">Nobel Foundation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th,_1895.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A paper with stylish handwriting on it with the title &quot;Testament&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg/220px-Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg/330px-Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg/440px-Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2965" data-file-height="2056" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th,_1895.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alfred Nobel's <a href="/wiki/Will_and_testament" title="Will and testament">will</a> stated that 94% of his total assets should be used to establish the Nobel Prizes.</div></div></div>
<p>According to his will and testament read in Stockholm on 30 December 1896, a foundation established by Alfred Nobel would reward those who serve humanity. The Nobel Prize was funded by Alfred Nobel's personal fortune. According to the official sources, Alfred Nobel bequeathed from the shares 94% of his fortune to the Nobel Foundation that now forms the economic base of the Nobel Prize.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Foundation" title="Nobel Foundation">Nobel Foundation</a> was founded as a private organization on 29 June 1900. Its function is to manage the finances and administration of the Nobel Prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz14_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz14-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In accordance with Nobel's <a href="/wiki/Will_and_testament" title="Will and testament">will</a>, the primary task of the Foundation is to manage the fortune Nobel left. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Nobel" title="Robert Nobel">Robert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ludvig_Nobel" title="Ludvig Nobel">Ludvig Nobel</a> were involved in the <a href="/wiki/Oil_business" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil business">oil business</a> in <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, and according to Swedish <a href="/wiki/Historian" title="Historian">historian</a> E. Bargengren, who accessed the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_family" title="Nobel family">Nobel family</a> <a href="/wiki/Archive" title="Archive">archive</a>, it was this "decision to allow withdrawal of Alfred's money from <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> that became the decisive factor that enabled the Nobel Prizes to be established".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Another important task of the Nobel Foundation is to market the prizes internationally and to oversee informal administration related to the prizes. The Foundation is not involved in the process of selecting the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_laureates" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel laureates">Nobel laureates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz15_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz15-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feldman16_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman16-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In many ways, the Nobel Foundation is similar to an <a href="/wiki/Investment_company" title="Investment company">investment company</a>, in that it invests Nobel's money to create a solid funding base for the prizes and the administrative activities. The Nobel Foundation is <a href="/wiki/Tax_exemption" title="Tax exemption">exempt from all taxes</a> in Sweden (since 1946) and from investment taxes in the United States (since 1953).<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz17-18_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz17-18-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1980s, the Foundation's investments have become more profitable and as of 31 December 2007, the assets controlled by the Nobel Foundation amounted to 3.628 billion Swedish <i>kronor</i> (c. US$560 million).<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz15-17_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz15-17-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the statutes, the Foundation consists of a board of five Swedish or Norwegian citizens, with its seat in Stockholm. The <a href="/wiki/Chairman" class="mw-redirect" title="Chairman">Chairman of the Board</a> is appointed by the Swedish <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_Sweden" title="Privy Council of Sweden">King in Council</a>, with the other four members appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustees</a> of the prize-awarding <a href="/wiki/Institutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Institutions">institutions</a>. An <a href="/wiki/Executive_director" title="Executive director">Executive Director</a> is chosen from among the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board members</a>, a Deputy Director is appointed by the King in Council, and two <a href="/wiki/Deputies" class="mw-redirect" title="Deputies">deputies</a> are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Trustees" class="mw-redirect" title="Trustees">trustees</a>. However, since 1995, all the members of the board have been chosen by the trustees, and the Executive Director and the Deputy Director appointed by the board itself. As well as the board, the Nobel Foundation is made up of the prize-awarding institutions (the Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences, the Nobel Assembly at Karolinska Institute, the Swedish Academy, and the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Committee" title="Norwegian Nobel Committee">Norwegian Nobel Committee</a>), the trustees of these institutions, and <a href="/wiki/Audit" title="Audit">auditors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz15-17_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz15-17-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_capital_and_cost">Foundation capital and cost</span></h4>
<p>The capital of the Nobel Foundation today is invested 50% in <a href="/wiki/Shares" class="mw-redirect" title="Shares">shares</a>, 20% <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a> and 30% other <a href="/wiki/Investments" class="mw-redirect" title="Investments">investments</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Hedge_funds" class="mw-redirect" title="Hedge funds">hedge funds</a> or <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate</a>). The distribution can vary by 10 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-dn20121202_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn20121202-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> At the beginning of 2008, 64% of the funds were invested mainly in American and European stocks, 20% in bonds, plus 12% in real estate and hedge funds.<sup id="cite_ref-handelsblatt2008_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handelsblatt2008-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, the total annual cost was approximately 120 million <a href="/wiki/Krone_(currency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Krone (currency)">krona</a>, with 50 million krona as the prize money. Further costs to pay institutions and persons engaged in giving the prizes were 27.4 million krona. The events during the Nobel week in Stockholm and Oslo cost 20.2 million krona. The administration, Nobel <a href="/wiki/Symposium" title="Symposium">symposium</a>, and similar items had costs of 22.4 million krona. The cost of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic Sciences">Economic Sciences</a> prize of 16.5 Million krona is paid by the <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Riksbank" title="Sveriges Riksbank">Sveriges Riksbank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dn20121202_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn20121202-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_prizes">First prizes</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%B6ntgen,_Wilhelm_Conrad_(1845-1923).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A black and white photo of a bearded man in his fifties sitting in a chair." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg/170px-R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg/255px-R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg/340px-R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="4920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%B6ntgen,_Wilhelm_Conrad_(1845-1923).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_R%C3%B6ntgen" title="Wilhelm Röntgen">Wilhelm Röntgen</a> received the first Physics Prize for his discovery of X-rays.</div></div></div>
<p>Once the Nobel Foundation and its guidelines were in place, the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Committee" title="Nobel Committee">Nobel Committees</a> began collecting nominations for the inaugural prizes. Subsequently, they sent a list of preliminary candidates to the prize-awarding institutions.
</p><p>The Nobel Committee's Physics Prize shortlist cited <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_R%C3%B6ntgen" title="Wilhelm Röntgen">Wilhelm Röntgen</a>'s discovery of <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">X-rays</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Lenard" title="Philipp Lenard">Philipp Lenard</a>'s work on <a href="/wiki/Cathode_ray" title="Cathode ray">cathode rays</a>. The Academy of Sciences selected Röntgen for the prize.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman134_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman134-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Leroy117-118_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leroy117-118-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In the last decades of the 19th century, many chemists had made significant contributions. Thus, with the Chemistry Prize, the Academy "was chiefly faced with merely deciding the order in which these scientists should be awarded the prize".<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz77_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz77-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The Academy received 20 nominations, eleven of them for <a href="/wiki/Jacobus_Henricus_van_%27t_Hoff" title="Jacobus Henricus van &#39;t Hoff">Jacobus van 't Hoff</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Crawford118_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crawford118-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Van 't Hoff was awarded the prize for his contributions in <a href="/wiki/Chemical_thermodynamics" title="Chemical thermodynamics">chemical thermodynamics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz81_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz81-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feldman205_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman205-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Swedish Academy chose the poet <a href="/wiki/Sully_Prudhomme" title="Sully Prudhomme">Sully Prudhomme</a> for the first Nobel Prize in Literature. A group including 42 Swedish writers, artists, and literary critics protested against this decision, having expected <a href="/wiki/Leo_Tolstoy" title="Leo Tolstoy">Leo Tolstoy</a> to be awarded.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz144_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz144-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Some, including <a href="/wiki/Burton_Feldman" title="Burton Feldman">Burton Feldman</a>, have criticised this prize because they consider Prudhomme a mediocre poet. Feldman's explanation is that most of the Academy members preferred <a href="/wiki/Victorian_literature" title="Victorian literature">Victorian literature</a> and thus selected a Victorian poet.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman69_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman69-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The first Physiology or Medicine Prize went to the German physiologist and microbiologist <a href="/wiki/Emil_von_Behring" title="Emil von Behring">Emil von Behring</a>. During the 1890s, von Behring developed an <a href="/wiki/Antitoxin" title="Antitoxin">antitoxin</a> to treat <a href="/wiki/Diphtheria" title="Diphtheria">diphtheria</a>, which until then was causing thousands of deaths each year.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman242-244_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman242-244-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Leroy233_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leroy233-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> went to the Swiss <a href="/wiki/Henry_Dunant" title="Henry Dunant">Jean Henri Dunant</a> for his role in founding the International <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Red Cross Movement</a> and initiating the Geneva Convention, and jointly given to French pacifist <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Passy" title="Frédéric Passy">Frédéric Passy</a>, founder of the Peace League and active with Dunant in the Alliance for Order and Civilization.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span></h3>
<p>In 1938 and 1939, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Third Reich</a> forbade three laureates from Germany (<a href="/wiki/Richard_Kuhn" title="Richard Kuhn">Richard Kuhn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Butenandt" title="Adolf Butenandt">Adolf Friedrich Johann Butenandt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Domagk" title="Gerhard Domagk">Gerhard Domagk</a>) from accepting their prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz23_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz23-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Each man was later able to receive the diploma and medal.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilhelm85_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilhelm85-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Even though Sweden was officially neutral during the Second World War, the prizes were awarded irregularly. In 1939, the Peace Prize was not awarded. No prize was awarded in any category from 1940 to 1942, due to the <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Norway" title="German occupation of Norway">occupation of Norway by Germany</a>. In the subsequent year, all prizes were awarded except those for literature and peace.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the occupation of Norway, three members of the Norwegian Nobel Committee fled into exile. The remaining members escaped persecution from the Germans when the Nobel Foundation stated that the Committee building in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a> was Swedish property. Thus it was a safe haven from the German military, which was not at war with Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams23_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams23-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> These members kept the work of the Committee going, but did not award any prizes. In 1944, the Nobel Foundation, together with the three members in exile, made sure that nominations were submitted for the Peace Prize and that the prize could be awarded once again.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz23_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz23-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prize_in_Economic_Sciences">Prize in Economic Sciences</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG/220px-Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG/330px-Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG/440px-Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Nobel laureates by country</div></div></div>
<p>In 1968, Sweden's central bank <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Riksbank" title="Sveriges Riksbank">Sveriges Riksbank</a> celebrated its 300th anniversary by donating a large sum of money to the Nobel Foundation to be used to set up a prize in honour of Alfred Nobel. The following year, the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Sveriges Riksbank Prize in Economic Sciences in Memory of Alfred Nobel</a> was awarded for the first time. The Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences became responsible for selecting laureates. The first laureates for the Economics Prize were <a href="/wiki/Jan_Tinbergen" title="Jan Tinbergen">Jan Tinbergen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ragnar_Frisch" title="Ragnar Frisch">Ragnar Frisch</a> "for having developed and applied dynamic models for the analysis of economic processes".<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman343_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman343-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz207_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz207-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The Board of the Nobel Foundation decided that after this addition, it would allow no further new prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz20_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz20-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Award_process">Award process</span></h2>
<p>The award process is similar for all of the Nobel Prizes, the main difference being who can make nominations for each of them.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman16-17_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman16-17-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
